  38. As I previously owned a Clarisonic Plus face and body system, I'm familiar with what a mechanical cleansing brush should be able to do. My Clarisonic system was returned to Sephora due to a problem with staying charged and the fact that while I liked using it, at around a cost of $200 it wasn't that much, if any, better than using a manual face brush. Since I like some of the Olay moisturizers as well as other high end products, I thought I'd give this brush a try. Sadly, this brush has such little power that it wouldn't even make a good toy. I struggled using it through two cleansings and gave up the third time and went back to my manual brushes. I have a soft $25 Shiseido brush and Sephora's $7 brush that's a bit firm, and they do a much better job than this Olay system. The Olay brush has a different method of action than the Clarisonic line. The Clarisonic brush heads move VERY little in sort of a pulsating action. The Olay brush head rotates around and around and tugs at your skin. It's a very odd sensation and one that I didn't like. I didn't have any trouble with the brush catching my pulled back hair, but the foam pad easily snagged and pulled small wisps each time I used it. If you're thinking about getting this, save yourself the trouble of returning it and don't bother. If you really want a power brush, I suggest saving your money, doing your research and buying a Clarisonic.

There are only two ways to shrink pores, one is to use peptides and be patient while following a healthy berry, fruits and veggies based diet with lots of water or you can conceal them with silicone based products like Loreal Collagen filler (whichdoes keep forehead wrinkles down wonderfully) or Esttee lauder Pore minimizer. The latter solution is mostly temporary. The peptides DO work in the long haul but require a two month wait and then you have to keep using them. Genefique or Lancer method are the best after trying almost all of them.<br /><br />I cannot offer many reviews of olay products as the anti-aging line is too thick for me so I preferred Neutrogena but now as I'm over 35, neutro. is not strong enough for me. This brush is still a great part of a regimen because it does keep the rest of your face very clean. My acne has been dramatically reduced along the lower cheeks, neck and jaw lines. Getting a few white heads means I can just brush them away and my dab of clearsil advanced which works in one night not a huge application applied for a week over skin not truly clean. After about two weeks I'm really happy as I'm finally breaking the breakout cycle that starts around my period.<br /><br />Like many on here I'm not ready to invest in a Clarisonic but will eventually. Having tested one out, I can say that his will not come close to replacing a clarisonic but will still keep you clean and hopefully reduce acne. My darker spots are starter to fade which is great but a Clarisonic, because it has ionic technology and sonic waves is going to get much deeper into the skin, kill bacteria better and stimulate the skin. It is like the difference between the old school interplak tooth brushes and the superior sonic care. One cleans the gums stimulating them (or tearing them if you were not careful) while the sonicare actually healed them and helps you retain youthful gum tissue. As for eyes, Clarisonic makes an applicator with sonic technology called Black Opal that is for use around the delicate eye are and is very pricey, Michael Todd organics eye sonic is half the price and actually as good if not much better.<br /><br />All in all Olay did a great job and this device, if used carefully is an inexpensive way to dramatically improve your skin.
